<div id="review_153270790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/153270790" />
    <a title="Reading Vacation" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation"><img alt="Reading Vacation" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341857406p2/5102733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Vacation" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Vacation" href="/user/show/5102733-reading-vacation">Reading Vacation</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/8606522-torn">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer153270790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6249365811522342947">REVIEW<br/><br/>I read these three books back-to-back-to-back on my Kindle. The story had me so engaged, that I could not put it down. I was reading in the car, at school, on my bed, at the dinner table, and in the media room. You could call it an obsession.<br/><br/>In this paranormal tale, Wendy learns at the age of seventeen that she is a troll. Oh, but she isn’t just ANY troll, her past is filled with mystery, deceit, and some unexpected ancestors. Amanda Hocking carefully twisted this plot with all sorts of su</span>
  <span id="freeText6249365811522342947" style="display:none">REVIEW<br /><br />I read these three books back-to-back-to-back on my Kindle. The story had me so engaged, that I could not put it down. I was reading in the car, at school, on my bed, at the dinner table, and in the media room. You could call it an obsession.<br /><br />In this paranormal tale, Wendy learns at the age of seventeen that she is a troll. Oh, but she isn’t just ANY troll, her past is filled with mystery, deceit, and some unexpected ancestors. Amanda Hocking carefully twisted this plot with all sorts of surprises. I guarantee that you have not read a series quite like this before.<br /><br />Plain and simple – Wendy rocks! She starts out unsure and confused. I mean, who wouldn’t be questioning things if they just found out they were a troll. The beauty lies in how Wendy grows and changes. As her confidence grows, she becomes the girl (err troll) she was always meant to be.<br /><br />Let’s talk romance. Wendy has more boy trolls after her than she keep track of. They are all nice in their own way, but they each have their unique traits. Finn is protective. Loki is a flirt. Tove is like a brother. I loved them all.<br /><br />If you are looking for a battle, you have come to the right place. Amanda Hocking has written some of the most epic battle scenes ever. Sure these scenes are filled with the physical battle, but they also contain the emotions behind the fight. They were so real that I could FEEL them.<br /><br />This series about trolls surprised and entertained me. I will definitely be looking for more Amanda Hocking books to read.<br /><br />RATING<br /><br />5 Loved<br /><br />COVER COMMENTS<br /><br />I like how the covers are so similar and work together to tell the story. I also love the turquoise and black because it has a mysterious feel to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6249365811522342947" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_280155653" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280155653" />
    <a title="Aiysha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7353959-aiysha"><img alt="Aiysha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413034139p2/7353959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280155653?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aiysha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aiysha" href="/user/show/7353959-aiysha">Aiysha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/8606522-torn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280155653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12761649711108780848">‘Torn’ starts from exactly where Switched is left off. Wendy after getting fed up with the life she has at the palace persuades Rys into taking her back to Matt, her host brother’s house.<br/><br/>‘Torn’ is more exciting as it introduces many more characters some more surprising than others but I would’nt want to give it away! More dangers are to come as the Vittra are aware where Wendy is and that she has reached the age and is capable of becoming queen. After complications, which consequence in Finn to </span>
  <span id="freeText12761649711108780848" style="display:none">‘Torn’ starts from exactly where Switched is left off. Wendy after getting fed up with the life she has at the palace persuades Rys into taking her back to Matt, her host brother’s house.<br /><br />‘Torn’ is more exciting as it introduces many more characters some more surprising than others but I would’nt want to give it away! More dangers are to come as the Vittra are aware where Wendy is and that she has reached the age and is capable of becoming queen. After complications, which consequence in Finn to leave, Wendy finds leaving as the only choice. However Wendy can’t hide anywhere, where she won’t be tracked by the Trylle – or the Vittra for that matter.<br /><br />More action-packed and more lively than Switched as Wendy escapes without knowing the consequences she’ll face. A hidden secret , which could effect Wendy’s whole future, is also revealed in Torn. Also a mysterious, handsome Vittra, Loki is not what he appears to be and Wendy cannot come to terms with why she wants to protect him and what exactly she feels for him. Surely she’s in love with Finn isn’t she?<br /><br />Wendy realizes that she can’t return to her original life and seeks out to change things around her to fit her taste – especially the unfairly old Monarchy that everyone must abide with.<br /><br />Amanda Hocking has created new atmospheres which were non-existent and the World of Trolls unravels innovative mysteries keeping the reader intrigued into the story.<br /><br />A lovely twist entwining secrets and upcoming events that untangle and reveal thrilling and captivating ideas that leave you imploring to read Ascend, the final chapter of the Trylle Trilogy.<br /><br />Overall an enjoyable read however sometimes I feel at times that Wendy’s love is forced and her actions contradict her personality and what she is expected to do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12761649711108780848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Meags" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8542123-meags"><img alt="Meags" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524277146p2/8542123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1718480491?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meags" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meags" href="/user/show/8542123-meags">Meags</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=borrowbox-and-cloudlibrary">borrowbox-and-cloudlibrary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=mf">mf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8542123-meags?shelf=royalty-and-nobility">royalty-and-nobility</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1718480491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12892767662354129026"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>That was a hell of a lot more enjoyable than book one (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12133821.Switched__Trylle___1_' title='Switched (Trylle, #1) by Amanda Hocking' rel='nofollow noopener'>Switched</a>). I'm now solidly immersed within the world of the Trylle and eager to witness Wendy's humble rise to Queendom. <br/><br/>With the exception of my disdain for all the "adults" in this story, and my hair pulling frustration at the gutless wonder that is Finn (this guy...ARGGGHHH!!!), I truly grew to love most of the characters in this story. I loved that Matt (Wendy's brother from her human host family) returned to play a much more su</span>
  <span id="freeText12892767662354129026" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />That was a hell of a lot more enjoyable than book one (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12133821.Switched__Trylle___1_" title="Switched (Trylle, #1) by Amanda Hocking" rel="nofollow noopener">Switched</a>). I'm now solidly immersed within the world of the Trylle and eager to witness Wendy's humble rise to Queendom. <br /><br />With the exception of my disdain for all the "adults" in this story, and my hair pulling frustration at the gutless wonder that is Finn (this guy...ARGGGHHH!!!), I truly grew to love most of the characters in this story. I loved that Matt (Wendy's brother from her human host family) returned to play a much more substantial and stabilising role in Wendy's recently upturned life. I also enjoyed getting to know Willa, Tove and Rhys a bit more, and I even liked Wendy's new Tracker (aka her bodyguard), Duncan. <br /><br />Considering my negative reactions to Finn and his "duty comes above all else" bullshit, it is no wonder that the introduction of Loki, the cocky and dashing Vittra Markis (Prince of the Trylle enemy), stole my heart. I'm shipping him and Wendy and I'm shipping them HARD! Let's make this happen, people.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12892767662354129026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_130365335" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130365335" />
    <a title="Vicki Keire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4129072-vicki-keire"><img alt="Vicki Keire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303673489p2/4129072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130365335?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicki Keire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicki Keire" href="/user/show/4129072-vicki-keire">Vicki Keire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/8606522-torn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130365335" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12932474575106330142">I've been thinking about boundaries and edges a lot lately since picking up Amanda Hocking's newest release Torn, which she was kind enough to let me review early. The title alone suggests such things: Edges. Boundaries. Thresholds. Wendy Everly and nearly everyone she cares about stands at one of these in Hocking's second installment of her acclaimed Trylle trilogy. Friends, family, enemies, and Wendy herself remain caught in cross-currents of political and class struggles, navigating complex p</span>
  <span id="freeText12932474575106330142" style="display:none">I've been thinking about boundaries and edges a lot lately since picking up Amanda Hocking's newest release Torn, which she was kind enough to let me review early. The title alone suggests such things: Edges. Boundaries. Thresholds. Wendy Everly and nearly everyone she cares about stands at one of these in Hocking's second installment of her acclaimed Trylle trilogy. Friends, family, enemies, and Wendy herself remain caught in cross-currents of political and class struggles, navigating complex personal ties that alternately bind and strangle, all the while confronting the eternal question of self-definition. Who is Wendy Everly? Who does she want to be, and at what cost to herself, to Forening, to her family and friends?<br /><br />These are not new dilemmas. Readers face them, or some variant of them, every single day. They are endemic to the human condition. And yet Amanda Hocking makes them not only new, but magical, distilling them into one not-quite human character who is wildness made flesh, a woman-girl who runs barefoot and wild-haired through woods and palaces alike, her sometimes angry, sometimes shy steps dogged by the sound of the baubles she loves and the scent of ancient magic in her blood. That, and the routine righteous rantings of an American teenager, for Wendy Everly is nothing if not doubly cursed. Or blessed. For therein lies one of Hocking's greatest gifts, and one she shares with her late great idol, filmmaker John Hughes: the ability to capture young adulthood as the threshold it is, that immortal breath between child and adult when all seems possible.<br /><br />What is it about the age of seventeen that makes everything so raw, so intense, and so magical? Hocking knows, and in Torn, as in all her books, she manages to pin it for a moment, if not capture it outright.<br /><br />Even mere mortals sense it. I know I do: At seventeen, I lay the wrong way on an old sofa in a darkened theatre inches away from a boy I loved so fiercely feelings pulsed between us like a living thing, an abyss so powerful we dared not move or speak its name. We lay pinned immobile instead, our backs where our butts should be, and looked up at the distant dull metal ceiling and invented constellations, awed by this new power between us. What was that thing, and why was it so powerful? What is the nature of the thing that makes usually obedient young people sneak out bedroom windows or refuse, out right, to stop seeing "that awful boy," even if it means losing the cell phone until social security kicks in? Hormones? First love? Lust? Rebellion? Need? Compelling explanations, and probably true, but I prefer Ms. Hocking's:<br /><br />Magic. In the threshold between child and adult, we all have a breath of magic in us. <br /><br />For Wendy Everly, the Trylle changeling heroine of Amanda Hocking's latest novel Torn, there is actual magic involved as she begins to master both her stubborn temper and her gifts of persuasion, telekenesis, and a few nifty new ones that make their presence known for the first time. But Wendy also must navigate the two most difficult experiences anyone, Trylle or not, ever has to face: love and family. As Wendy matures (delightfully so, in fact), love and family only become more and more complicated. Her own life choices are highly restricted by unfair rules and a racist class system she neither supports nor helped to create, and yet she finds herself expected to not only obey this system of laws, but to one day be its supreme enforcer. If she doesn't, her world will be engulfed in a brutal war, killing many of the people she loves.<br /><br />And I thought picking a college was hard.<br /><br />Within her limited range of choices, Wendy makes good ones. In this sequel to Switched, we watch as Wendy cobbles together some acceptance of her past and her dual heritage, both Trylle and human. Not ready to forgive and forget (nor should she be), Wendy nonetheless comes to understand Elora, if not love her, even as she remains unapologetically attached to her human family. She carves out pockets of peace for herself in Forening: a patch of garden, a view of the sky. She ventures beyond the palace to see how other Trylle live, where the societal cost of her people's parasitic existence becomes real for her in uncomfortably personal ways. She goes where she shouldn't and speaks (er...yells?) when she should be silent. We learn quite a lot more about Troll culture, including its history, the rival Vittras, and the ancient Tryllic language.<br /><br />I've got to give Amanda Hocking props for her research here. In my research on her research for the Trylle trilogy (if that made any sense), she at one point wrote about how the genesis for the series came from a line in a book about Scandanavian mythology, and the idea kind of caught fire from there. I was intrigued; there is nothing new under the sun, after all, but never before have I encountered an engaging YA read about trolls. In fact, I don't think I've ever read about trolls as anything other than rock-eating monsters. I had to know more. <br /><br />***Alert: Research blatherings ahead. Romance resumes exactly one paragraph below***So when a group of characters in Torn encounter an ancient tome written entirely in Tryllic, the ancient tongue of these elegant, enlightened beings, I was stunned to see that Hocking had phonetically written it in Cyrillic letters, a variant of Old Church Slavonic, which would have been what the region's oldest myths were first recorded in. Lose you? Bore you to death? Sorry. It's just that she's obviously done some serious research here, chosen authenticity over fluff, and my pulse raced more than a little when Wendy got her hands on that lovely Cyrillic Tryllic. The research that goes into crafting a well-written book so often slips under the radar, and I didn't want to let this one slide. Indie books are often criticized for basic grammatical/typographical errors, and yet here we have one that not only evades these most basic of indie writing pitfalls, but reaches beyond into the kind of deep world building that marks territory previously cordoned off only for "serious" writers. You don't get much more serious than Old Church Slavonic; the last book I read to tackle it was by Orson Scott Card, and even he didn't reproduce its actual alphabet. It's one of the reasons I love her writing: it maintains the fresh, experimental voice of the indie writer with occassional forays into the realms of "serious literature," and yet manages to be, above all, entertaining. Excellent, Ms. Hocking. We need more like you. So then. Where were we?<br /><br />Romance? Let's talk Finn.<br /><br />Yes, Finn. He's back, with his fierce black eyes and overwhelming protective instincts. He's still determined to protect Wendy's honor from the danger he poses to her as a lowly tracker. (She's really gotta do something about that caste system.) And although all the elements of a great romance with Finn are there, from sizzling jealousy to help-I-can't-breathe-'cause-you're-looking-at-me moments to daring Vittra rescues, Hocking introduces a maddening new element: competition. See, Wendy's grown up a bit. She's coming to terms with this Princess thing. She's more self-confident and her hair has better manners. She's making peace with her wardrobe. She's taking less crap, and when she gives an order, it's usually obeyed. And the boys are noticing. All of them. There are the ususal suspects, of course, from Switched, including Finn and, to an extent, Rhys, but we also meet a sexy new one. He's hot (very- think motorcycles and leather jackets), he's edgy, and if your mama didn't warn you about him, she just hasn't met him yet. He can offer Wendy the one thing no one else ever has, or maybe even can: complete and total freedom, from Forening, from the Vittra, from everything.<br /><br />And then there's Tove.<br /><br />Tove, you say? WTF? I know, I know. But don't count him out. Tove is instrumental in this second installment of the Trylle trilogy; because of his Trylle gifts, in many ways, he's the closest thing Wendy has to an equal. He makes an excellent teacher, pushing Wendy to the limits of her powers even as he reiterates, over and over, the need for change and his confidence in her abilty to bring it about. Hocking exercises a deft touch here. I mentally conflated "Tove" with "Toad" for a variety of reasons that should be obvious to Switched readers, but in Torn, suddenly I turned the page to find an altogether decent guy. It's like that moment when your best guy pal for like, forever, whips off his shirt one hot summer afternoon when you've been mowing lawns or something equally grimy and you just sit there, quietly stunned, wondering when the hell the fairies stole your dorky friend away and replaced him with someone you would actually date. Awkward, but also cool and sexy in a squirmy, embarrassing kind of way. And an incredible feat of character building for any writer. Bravo.<br /><br />All in all, Torn offers up a thoroughly entertaining read with all the things we have come to expect from Amanda Hocking's writing: engaging characters with fresh voices; a well-crafted world; solid writing with professional editing and packaging; an energy and connection with her readers that is somewhat harder to define. She continues to be, in my opinion, one of the very best indie writers in the industry: edgy, hard working, whimsical. I'm very much looking forward to the third installment in her Trylle series, along with whatever other offerings she throws our way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12932474575106330142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_344868070" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344868070" />
    <a title="Arooj " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4466525-arooj"><img alt="Arooj " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553208603p2/4466525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344868070?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arooj " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arooj " href="/user/show/4466525-arooj">Arooj </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344868070" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16923001043959324746">Plot wise? A pretty good sequel.<br/>Character wise? No. Especially how Wendy acted.<br/><br/><b>The Good</b><br/>- There was a lot more plot development than the last book. The first book, Switched, consisted mainly of Wendy just learning to be a Princess, and it got a little boring. However, this wasn't entirely like that.<br/> <br/>- I enjoyed learning more about the history between the Trylle and the Vittra. I now understand why they're enemies and how serious the situation is. I also see the Vittra in a new light now. They're </span>
  <span id="freeText16923001043959324746" style="display:none">Plot wise? A pretty good sequel.<br />Character wise? No. Especially how Wendy acted.<br /><br /><b>The Good</b><br />- There was a lot more plot development than the last book. The first book, Switched, consisted mainly of Wendy just learning to be a Princess, and it got a little boring. However, this wasn't entirely like that.<br /> <br />- I enjoyed learning more about the history between the Trylle and the Vittra. I now understand why they're enemies and how serious the situation is. I also see the Vittra in a new light now. They're still not the good guys, but I can see their reasons.<br /> <br /><b>The Bad</b><br />- The ending felt a little abrupt. I'm not a huge fan of cliffhangers, but I'd prefer that over a boring ending. It should make me want to read the next book in the series right away. I didn't even know it was the end until I flipped the page.<br /> <br /><b>The In-Betweens</b><br />- From the synopsis, it's obvious that there will be a love triangle with a new character. I didn't mind this because the previous book had a little hint of a love triangle with Rhys, which would've been really awkward. But that ended. I was worried that the love triangle will ruin the romance by becoming one of those ones where the main girl instantly falls in love with another guy and keeps thinking which one to pick. Fortunately, that didn't happen here. Wendy and Loki do have an attraction towards each other, but it doesn't developed to much more until near the end, which made sense to me. The romance between Wendy and Finn on the other hand barely develops. They spend the whole book either ignoring the other person, or arguing when they do talk. Not exactly romantic. Honestly, I prefer Loki and Wendy over Finn and Wendy right now.<br /> <br /><b>The Characters</b><br />- Wendy was a big part of why I didn't like this book that much. She was kind of selfish and her attitude towards her situation wasn't confident. Here are three reasons:<br /> <br />1. I was really annoyed at how she kept saying that she didn't want to be a troll Princess and rebelled against everything. Now, I'm glad that she was fighting for her happiness, I understand how she must have felt. But instead of complaining constantly about how unfair all of this was, she should've just accepted that fact that she's a damn Princess, and nothing will change that. Instead o fighting it, she should've found ways to cope with it. She kept disregarding the fact that their enemies were after her, and that she can totally take them in herself. Even though she was attacked by them two times, and both times she had needed help.<br /> <br />2. The second thing that annoyed me was how she kept using her persuasion on others. She said she doesn't like doing it and stopped later on, but the times she did use it seemed unnecessary. For example, at the end of the first book she used her persuasion on Rhys to get him to come with her, even though he was strongly against it. She could've respected his decision, but no. Her reasons might have been for good, but it wasn't her right to make that decision. I understand if she had to use her persuasion on someone for an emergency, but the times she used it on Rhys and Duncan were not emergencies.<br /> <br />3. For the majority of the book, Wendy was either sad, angry, or really, really tired. Seeing as how this book is written in first person, it was really depressing. Wendy didn't sound anything at all like a brave girl with powers like others claimed.<br /> <br />Wendy does get better in the second half of the book though. She makes smart decisions and tries her best to handle her situation. I hope she continues to get better like this in the third book.<br /> <br />- Finn barely develops in this book. I'm honestly not liking his character. I'm not really into the "brooding, serious, hot hunk" types of guys anymore. They're so...boring. Finn was all business, except for a couple times when his mask slips. But, as always, he covers it up and denies his true feelings. I have a feeling that in the last book he'll suddenly transform into someone who doesn't care about his place anymore and whisks the Princess away. I hope he's more realistic than that.<br /><br />- Loki was really fun to read. I thought he'd be another mean, scary dude because he's a Vittra, but Loki was quite the opposite. He was all fun, flirty, and full of wit. Not to mention totally nice. I definitely prefer him to Finn.<br /> <br />- I still think that Elora is a bitch but after hearing her story, I feel sympathetic towards her. I now get why she's so strict. What she went through, wow, she was really brave. <br /> <br /><b>Recommended?</b><br />In some ways, this book was better than the first, but in other ways, it wasn't. I was going to give a higher rating, but I couldn't bring myself to give it anything more than three stars. But it's worth continuing the series. I think it has some great build up for the third and last book.<br /><br />Looking forward to reading Ascend soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16923001043959324746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1134079466" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134079466" />
    <a title="Norah Una Sumner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28782884-norah-una-sumner"><img alt="Norah Una Sumner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569421053p2/28782884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1134079466?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norah Una Sumner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norah Una Sumner" href="/user/show/28782884-norah-una-sumner">Norah Una Sumner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fantasy lovers,people who read switched</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=family-theme">family-theme</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=drama-llama">drama-llama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=love">love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=read-in-serbian">read-in-serbian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28782884-norah-una-sumner?shelf=super-nice-authors">super-nice-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134079466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6588073178473891647">Okay,I admit - this one was way better than the first part.<br/>Even Elora is more likeable and approachable.We basically get more information about Wendy's family and the constant war between the Vitrra and Trylle.<br/>Summary of the characters:<br/>-Finn is being a huge freaking jackass.(but because he cares,duh!...I swear,I was praying through the whole book that Wendy will just forget about him.)<br/>-Villa and Matt are spending more time together.<br/>-Rhys is pretty much forgotten.<br/>-Tove is being awesome as always.</span>
  <span id="freeText6588073178473891647" style="display:none">Okay,I admit - this one was way better than the first part.<br />Even Elora is more likeable and approachable.We basically get more information about Wendy's family and the constant war between the Vitrra and Trylle.<br />Summary of the characters:<br />-Finn is being a huge freaking jackass.(but because he cares,duh!...I swear,I was praying through the whole book that Wendy will just forget about him.)<br />-Villa and Matt are spending more time together.<br />-Rhys is pretty much forgotten.<br />-Tove is being awesome as always.<br />-Dancan is being very nice(as I expected him to be).<br />-Loki,the new badass flirty Vittra,is pretty cool and amusing.( I mean,Finn,honey,you can learn something from this guy.)<br />-our Wendy is becoming more aware of her duties and her destiny.(she finally wants to improve her powers and learn more about the history of her kingdom.)<br /><br />Things I liked in this book:<br /><b>1.)</b> Tove.He is so nice and supportive and wants to help Wendy with everything.He is even okay with their wedding and tries to be cool about it and make her more comfortable.<br /><b>2.)</b> That we finally have some explanation about the Vittra and Trylle relationship.I'm really glad that we got to see that Elora is not entirely a cold-hearted bitch and that she made so many sacrifices to save her kingdom and her people.<br /><b>3.</b> Wendy/Loki relationship.Since I pretty much hate Finn and I know that Tove will always be a friend to her,I was so freaking happy when we got another character who Wendy could end up with.He seems like a very fun,interesting,honest guy although he is a Vittra.(''devilishly handsome, debonair young men who come to sweep rebellious princesses of their feet'')10 FOR YOU LOKI STAAD,YOU GO LOKI STAAD!<br /><br />Things I didn't like in this book:<br /><b>1.)</b> The lack of depth in this story.I don't know,I felt like I was just reading basic information about the characters and not what they actually feel.<br /><br />Favourite quotes:<br /><br />“I don't care where I come from or who you are.<b> I can make you happy, and you make me happy</b>. We could have a happily ever after.” <br /><br />"Wendy!" Loki leaned out into the hall, so far it made him grimace with pain. "If you're right and the next time we see each other is when our kingdoms are at war, you and I never will be.<b>I'll never fight you</b>.That I can promise you.” </span>
  <a data-text-id="6588073178473891647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1754117118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1754117118" />
    <a title="Dilushani Jayalath" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42055091-dilushani-jayalath"><img alt="Dilushani Jayalath" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468042052p2/42055091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1754117118?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dilushani Jayalath" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dilushani Jayalath" href="/user/show/42055091-dilushani-jayalath">Dilushani Jayalath</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781447205708" href="/book/show/9716824-torn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1754117118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7872446953153517355">I love the fact I waited almost more than two years to read the second book after reading the first one.<br/><br/>First of all, it's because when i finished the first one I had thoroughly fallen in love with Finn. So I couldn't bear to have another guy jump in between their romance at all. I read some reviews before hand and saw that some new "Loki" was going to disrupt everything and thus stopped reading. Recently while going through my shelves I saw this again and also saw that I purchased the first two</span>
  <span id="freeText7872446953153517355" style="display:none">I love the fact I waited almost more than two years to read the second book after reading the first one.<br /><br />First of all, it's because when i finished the first one I had thoroughly fallen in love with Finn. So I couldn't bear to have another guy jump in between their romance at all. I read some reviews before hand and saw that some new "Loki" was going to disrupt everything and thus stopped reading. Recently while going through my shelves I saw this again and also saw that I purchased the first two books in the Kanin chronicles too so I thought "why not?" and gave it a chance and boy was I not happy.<br /><br />The story was enthralling. Everything had the perfect setting for a teenage supernatural story and I loved it. I haven't read this genre in a very long time and honestly I was starting to find it pretty boring, so this was a very pleasant surprise. Rather, me liking it was a pleasant surprise. <br /><br />First thing first, I loved that "some new Loki"!!! Like really loved him. By the time I started this I had generally forgotten Finn until he popped up in the book, I had completely forgotten his name too. SO it was pretty good start for me. Loki was everything good that Finn just couldn't be. And I loved it.<br /><br />The characters were not likeable but rather loveable. What can I say? Looks like I still have that squealing teenage girl in me. I loved Matt, Duncan, Willa, Tove, pretty much everyone.<br /><br />The only bad thing to be noted was how Wendy kept jumping between Like and Finn. Other than that perfect for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7872446953153517355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('G6dcLFI7I5aydcVSNVIEcHWemYIrAtOez41SqcP+n/rI+6ZOksa31URfwwhvOia+vLxnOYOAZbeVoAv+bOVmkw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hLGCA4OKX4gLSNWDtMgPXp8gd5YhP/h0zaxbqNodOCFX7XhhQ3fLy/1i09nuoC2QVgKJLYm9Tl2XgQL/dQbBSA==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText14565017738247719510" style="display:none">AMANDA HOCKING is the author of over twenty young adult novels, including the New York Times bestselling Trylle Trilogy and Kanin Chronicles. Her love of pop culture and all things paranormal influence her writing. She spends her time in Minnesota, taking care of her menagerie of pets and working on her next book.<br /><br />Several of her books have made the New York Times Bestsellers list. Her zombie series, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/hollowland-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hollows</a>, has been adapted into a graphic novel by Dynamite. She has published over twenty novels, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/48928-trylle&gt; the Trylle Trilogy&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kanin Chronicles</a>, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/watersong-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">the Watersong quartet</a>, <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/amanda-hockings-books/my-blood-approves-series/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blood Approves series</a>, the Valkyrie duology<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/150484-valkyrie" rel="nofollow noopener"></a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25184362-freeks#other_reviews" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Freeks</em>
</a>.<br /><br />Her next books are the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47590299-the-lost-city" rel="nofollow noopener"> Omte Origins</a>, a trilogy set in the world of the Trylle and Kanin. The first book <em> The Lost City</em> will be out July 7, 2020, and the second book <em> The Morning Flower </em> will be out August 5, 2020. <br /><br />For more info about her and her books, here are some other places to check out and ways to contact her:<br /><br />Website: <a href="http://www.hockingbooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.hockingbooks.com</a><br /><br />Amazon Author Page: <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Amanda-Hocking/e/B003H4L762" rel="nofollow noopener">amazon.com/author/amandahocking</a><br /><br />Instagram: <a href="https://instagram.com/amanda_hocking/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram.com/amanda_hocking/</a><br /><br />YouTube: <a href="https://www.youtube.com/aehocking" rel="nofollow noopener">www.youtube.com/aehocking</a><br /><br /><br />Pinterest: <a href="http://www.pinterest.com/aehocking/" rel="nofollow noopener">www.pinterest.com/aehocking/</a><br /></span>
